6.7
Comparison of results from mixed cable type scenarios
As per the observations made, certain interesting findings are discovered for the mixed cable type
scenarios of distinct grid types. However, to determine the contrast between these results and the
previous designed grid type scenarios, a comparison is required across all the modelled mixed
cable type scenarios in terms of the observed optimal locations for placing digitized secondary
substations and their corresponding benefits in terms of ENS reduction (%). This comparison is
presented in this section.
Optimal substation placement locations
Figure 6.9 illustrates the optimal solutions for digitized secondary substation placement in mixed
cable type scenarios, grouped based on their corresponding chosen feeder. The optimal solutions
for the placement of the first digitized secondary substation are plotted in figure 6.9a, while the
optimal solutions for the placement of the second digitized secondary substation are plotted in
figure 6.9b. The x-axis represents the modeled scenarios, while the y-axis represents the substation
number of the secondary substations in the test grid. This comparison provides a clear visualization
of the variation in the optimal substation locations for mixed cable type scenarios in different
feeders, as well as the similarity and differences in optimal solutions between scenarios.
• The optimal placement for the first digitized secondary substation for scenarios grouped under the
same chosen feeder is observed to be consistent across all modeled mixed cable type scenarios,
as seen in figure 6.9a. These optimal locations are substations with open tie points connecting
them to neighboring feeders, except for scenarios grouped under feeder 4, where no global best
location for placing a digitized secondary substation is found and therefore the substation in the
middle of the feeder is fixed to be the optimal location.
The optimal location for the first digitized secondary substation in the mixed cable type scenarios
is seen not to be affected by the mix and location of load and generation sources, similar to the
observation in the previous grid type scenarios. Furthermore, the change in failure frequencies
of the MV lines in each scenario as a result of different cable types being present in different
clusters within a feeder does not seem to influence the optimal placement of the first digitized
secondary substation. This suggests that the placement of the first digitized secondary substation
in a feeder network is independent of the influence drivers defined for the distinct grid types in
this study. It is always the substation with the open tie-point connection to its neighbouring
feeders.
• The optimal solution for placing the second digitized secondary substation for scenarios grouped
under the same feeder for placement is mostly observed to be the same for mixed cable type
scenarios of city and suburban grid types, as seen in figure 6.9b. However, there are some
energy island mixed cable type scenarios that showed variation in the optimal solution for placing
a second digitized secondary substation, especially those grouped under feeder 1 and feeder
2. This observation suggests that there may be a correlation between high renewable energy
penetration and mixed cable types in a feeder, and the optimal location for placing a second
digitized secondary substation. However, further evaluation is required to gain a more clear
understanding of their relationship.

Figure 6.9: Optimal digitized substation placement location for mixed cable type scenarios

==PAGE:87==
Percentage ENS reduction
The ENS reduction (%) upon placing a digitized secondary substation in the modelled mixed cable
type scenarios is represented in Figure 6.10. This figure helps to determine the benefit of placing a
digitized secondary substation in each scenario and rank the mixed cable type scenarios accordingly.
By ranking the scenarios, we can investigate the impact of the mixing of cable types with different
failure frequencies on their priority for digitization through the placement of a digitized substation.
The results are presented in two bar graphs, where the x-axis represents the modeled scenarios and
the y-axis represents the ENS reduction (%). The scenarios are arranged in descending order based
on their ENS reduction (%), providing a ranking of the scenarios in terms of their benefit from
placing a digitized secondary substation. The first plot shows the scenarios grouped by their grid
types and ranked by their ENS reduction (%), as depicted in figure 6.10a. The second plot shows
the scenarios grouped by their chosen feeder type for digitized secondary substation placement and
ranked by their ENS reduction (%), as illustrated in figure 6.10b.
• Ranking the percentage ENS reduction for the mixed cable type modelled scenarios when viewed
according to their grid type reveals an interesting outcome as shown in figure 6.10a. The analysis
of the ENS reduction (%) upon placing a digitized secondary substation in the mixed cable type
scenarios shows a lack of clear hierarchy in terms of distinct grid type scenarios. The top three
scenarios with the highest ENS reduction (%) are observed to be a mix of city, suburban, and
energy island grid types, namely scenarios E_mix cable_8, CT_mix_cable 8, and S_mix_cable
8. This is in contrast to the previous grid type scenarios, where a clear hierarchy in ranking was
observed for city type grid scenarios followed by suburban and energy island type grid scenarios.
Furthermore, it is notable that the ENS reduction (%) for mixed cable type scenarios is signifi-
cantly lower than that of previous grid type scenarios. The scenarios that underwent the mixing
of cable types to form mixed cable scenarios appear to provide less benefit in terms of ENS re-
duction (%). For instance, the city type grid scenario CT8, which is one of the scenarios grouped
under feeder 2, is seen to provide the highest benefit of 52.26 % ENS reduction among previous
grid type scenarios. However, when the same scenario are subjected to multiple cable types in
feeder 2 to form the mixed cable scenario CT_mix_cable 8, the ENS reduction (%) decreased to
16.3%. This is an interesting observation which suggests that prioritizing scenarios with cables
that have higher failure rates may lead to greater ENS reduction (%).
• The ranking of the ENS reduction (%) based on the chosen feeder for digitized substation place-
ment reveals an interesting pattern among the mixed cable type scenarios. Figure 6.10b shows
that the scenarios grouped under feeder 2 is seen to have the highest rankings in most cases. This
is followed by scenarios grouped under feeder 1, feeder 3, and finally feeder 4.
This observation is significant as it indicates that feeder characteristics play a critical role in de-
termining the ENS reduction achievable by placing a digitized secondary substation. This obser-
vation differs from the previous grid type scenario ranking, where grid types (city, suburban, and
energy island) are the most significant or dominant factor towards availing the maximum benefit
in terms of ENS reduction (%). The ranking of mixed cable type scenarios clearly indicates that
feeder characteristics, such as length, nodes, and tie-point connections with neighboring feeders,
become the dominant factor for ENS reduction (%) and thereby needs to be prioritized based on
these characteristics.

CHAPTER 7
Discussion: Interpretation and
evaluation of results
The optimal location for placing the first digitized secondary substation in a feeder network is de-
termined to be the one with an open tie point connection to neighboring feeders, as observed across
all modeled scenarios shown in section 6.4. This finding is consistent with previous studies and
indicates that placing a digitized secondary substation at the open tie point location can minimize
energy supply interruptions and facilitate optimal network reconfiguration during faults, resulting
in optimal power restoration. Furthermore, it is observed that the influence drivers defined to cre-
ate distinct grid types which are the load and generation resources, as well as their locations within
the current and neighboring feeders, do not appear to influence the optimal location for the place-
ment of the first digitized secondary substation in a feeder network. Additionally, the same trend
of optimal solutions when it comes to placing the first digitized secondary substation in a feeder
network is observed for the modelled mixed cable type scenarios as shown in section 6.7. Having
a mix of cable types of different failure frequencies (two in this case study) is seen not to influence
the optimal location for the placement of the first digitized secondary substation in the modelled
scenarios.
Unlike the situation where placing the first digitized substation showed the same optimal location
across the three distinct grid types for the same feeder type, that isn’t the observation while placing a
second digitized secondary substation as shown in section 6.4. The optimal location for the second
digitized secondary substation is seen to vary for the three distinct grid types as observed in figure
6.4b. This is an interesting observation which shows that having different load and generation
source mix does seem to influence the placement of a second digitized secondary substation.
This observation might pique the interest of DSOs, when they plan to introduce a second digitized
secondary substation into a feeder network. The results of this study show that the placement of
the second digitized secondary substation is not always at the substation with an open tie-point
location, unlike in the case of placing the first digitized secondary substation in the feeder network.
The optimal location for the second digitized substation is therefore seen to be influenced by the
type of grid which basically refers to the influence drivers defined for a particular grid. To gain a
clearer understanding of the influence of these drivers, a more detailed study of their interactions
with each other is required.
Another key observation is that the optimal solutions for grid type scenarios grouped under the same
feeder type for placement of second digitized substations remain consistent 6.4. This suggests that
the location for placing a second digitized secondary substation within a feeder does not seem to
Modelling and optimal planning of digitized and automated secondary substation
75
==PAGE:90==
be influenced by location of the influence drivers defined for the respective grid types. However,
it is observed in the case of mixed cable type scenarios that the optimal solution for placing a
second digitized secondary substation is seen to vary even for scenarios grouped under the same
feeder type for placement of digitized substations 6.7. This shows that having a difference in
failure frequencies within a feeder network seems to have an influence in the optimal location for
second digitized secondary substation. So a change in the characteristics of the feeder, in this case
the failure frequencies for the lines due to multiple cable types, seems to bring a change in the
optimal solution for the placement of a second digitized secondary substation. Therefore, it is not
possible to generalize the optimum location for placing a second digitized secondary substation
across all the modelled mixed cable scenarios, a detailed study on the feeder type characteristics
and its influence on optimal placement location for digitized secondary substation is essential to
make a conclusion.
Additionally, it is observed that although the optimal location for placement of the second digitized
secondary substation does not get influenced by the location of the influence drivers. However,
when comparing among the scenarios grouped under the same feeder for digitized secondary sub-
station placement, it is observed that the optimal location differs among the distinct grid types. For
example the optimal location for the placement of the second digitized secondary substation in sce-
narios grouped under feeder 1 for city type grid is not the same as the optimal location found in the
case of scenarios of energy island type grid as shown in section 6.4. This suggests that the type of
influence drivers in a grid does influence the optimal placement of the second digitized secondary
substation. Although this observation is made, the current optimization approach and its analy-
sis are limited and cannot provide a clear answer to this observation. Therefore, a more in-depth
correlation study between the type of influence drivers and their impact on optimal placement is
necessary to understand the relation.
Another important thing that needs to be mentioned here is that simultaneously optimizing the
placement of two digitized secondary substations in a feeder network can be another approach to
optimally place multiple substations, as it can help to evenly split the network and optimize the
placement of the substations. This approach could involve placing a digitized secondary substation
at the first third part of the feeder and another at the last third part, as proposed in [13]. However,
this approach would be inefficient from the perspective of the optimization approach utilized in
this thesis work. In this study, the ENS of the network is calculated by individually digitizing each
secondary substation and performing a reliability assessment in PowerFactory. Performing a reli-
ability assessment in PowerFactory for each possible combination of simultaneously placing two
digitized secondary substations would be impractical, as it would take a lot of time to evaluate each
case. Furthermore, individually digitizing each secondary substation and performing a reliability
assessment one at a time would lead to a very long run time for the optimization of a single grid
type scenario.
Additionally, It is also imperative to mention that the focus of this study case was on determining
the optimal placement of a digitized secondary substation in a feeder network for the purpose of
enhancing reliability and aiding in optimal network reconfiguration during fault conditions in the
MV lines. The observations summarized for the optimal placement location for digitized secondary
substations are limited to this approach.
Further, ranking the distinct grid type scenarios on the basis of the ENS reduction (%) on placing
one digitized secondary substation projects that the highest benefit in terms of ENS reduction (%)
which translates to minimization in interruption of energy supply is observed for the city grid
type scenarios as shown in section 6.4. The city grid type scenarios considered in this study are
representative of urban areas with old cables of high failure frequency and high load levels in
76
Modelling and optimal planning of digitized and automated secondary substation
==PAGE:91==
certain secondary substations, resulting in a concentration of load in specific areas of the feeder.
Further, among the three modelled grid types a clear hierarchy in terms of benefit in placing a
digitized secondary substation is observed. The highest benefit was observed for city grid followed
by suburban and energy island grids.
In the case of mixed cable type scenarios, when ranked and grouped by their ENS reduction (%),
it showed interesting results. The rankings showed a lack of clear hierarchy among the grid types
as shown in section 6.7. This suggests that when a grid is composed of a mix of cable types with
varying failure probabilities, it is difficult to prioritize digitized secondary substation placement
on the basis of a particular type of grid. However, when the scenarios are ranked and grouped
by the feeders chosen for the placement of the digitized secondary substation, some degree of
grouping among scenarios are observed. Notably, most of the scenarios in which feeder 2 are
selected for digitized substation placement provided the highest ENS reduction, followed by feeder
1, feeder 3, and finally feeder 4. Feeder 2 by design is more long as it has more substations and MV
lines in the network. The results suggest that selecting feeder 2 for placing a digitized secondary
substation provides the greatest benefit in terms of ENS reduction (%), indicating that the feeder
length becomes more relevant when it consists of a mix of cable types of potentially different
failure frequencies. Therefore, careful consideration of feeder characteristics is necessary when
prioritizing feeder types for placing digitized secondary substations.
It is important to mention that these results are based on a case study defined for analysis. Therefore,
the approach taken in the study is limited in its scope. In reality, the interaction between various
feeder characteristics is complex and may affect the benefits gained in terms of improvements in
reliability differently. Therefore, future studies should focus on examining the influence of feeder
characteristics on prioritization of grids for reliability improvements in detail.
Furthermore, the fact that mixing cable types can result in blurring the clear hierarchy of prioritiza-
tion among distinct grid types motivates the need for more data analysis and a thorough evaluation
of individual cable failure rates. However, such data is currently not adequately present. The
observed influence of failure frequencies on ENS suggests that using an average failure rate for
the analysis might not provide the complete picture. Hence, a comparative study between ENS
for cables with average failure frequencies and cables with known, detailed failure frequencies
could be of interest. This would help to gain a better understanding of the effect of cable types on
the reliability of the grid and provide insights into the optimal placement of digitized secondary
substations.
It is also important to note that the ranking of different grid type scenarios in this study are based
on the ENS reduction benefits (%) observed upon placing the first digitized secondary substation
in the feeder network. This is because the observations showed only a small benefit in terms of
ENS reduction for the optimal placement of the second digitized secondary substation. However,
in the future, ranking grid types for the placement of the second digitized distribution system may
be of interest.
Modelling and optimal planning of digitized and automated secondary substation
77
==PAGE:92==
CHAPTER 8
Conclusion
The project has demonstrated the impact of digitizing distribution networks through optimal place-
ment and rollout of digitized secondary substations in distribution networks. The results have led to
two main conclusions. Firstly, the optimal location for introducing a digitized secondary substation
within a feeder network has been found to be at the substation with an open tie-point connection
to neighboring feeders. The study has shown that the various mix of load and generation profiles,
and their locations within the feeders, do not affect the optimal location. These findings highlight
the importance of open tie-point connections in feeders for optimal placement and rollout of digi-
tized secondary substations. Secondly, the project has also shown that prioritization of particular
grid type for digitized secondary substation placement should consider factors such as high load
level concentrations and high failure rate cables, which need to be given the highest priority. In
the context of this study, an urban city grid with high load level concentration and high failure rate
cables is to be prioritized for placing a digitized secondary substation.
In addition to the main conclusions, the study has also derived some subsidiary conclusions that
require further investigation and analysis for future studies. The placement of a second digitized
secondary substation within a feeder that already has a digitized secondary substation seemed to
be influenced by various influence drivers for the grid type, such as the mix of load and generation
sources. Even for grid types with the same feeder structure, the optimal location for placing a
second digitized secondary substation seemed to vary, indicating the importance of load and gen-
eration mix that constitute the grid type. This observation is important for Distribution System
Operators (DSOs), as they may encounter situations where they need to add a digitized substation
into a grid that already has one. Therefore, future research can explore the influence of these fac-
tors on the optimal placement of the second digitized secondary substation in a feeder network.
Further, the project also showed the relevance of feeder length in prioritization of a grid type es-
pecially when the feeder has a mix of different cable types of different failure frequencies. The
sensitivity analysis study drew an observation that the benefit of ENS reduction was seen to be
grouped according to the feeder type. This gives a strong indication for future researchers to in-
vestigate the relation between failure probabilities and feeder structure, as the sensitivity analysis
of the grid towards cable types have revealed that feeder characteristics can influence the optimal
placement location for the digitized secondary substations and the benefits achieved in terms of
minimizing disruptions in energy supply.
8.1
Project contribution
The project has made several contributions to the field of optimal planning and rollout of digitized
secondary substation. Firstly, a methodology to model a digitized secondary substation capable of
78
Modelling and optimal planning of digitized and automated secondary substation
==PAGE:93==
optimal network reconfiguration in the event of a fault for optimal power restoration is proposed.
Secondly, a novel framework for developing distribution grid type scenarios in accordance with
the Danish national projections for distribution networks in PowerFactory with the help of Python
is presented. The developed workflow for modeling various distribution grid types can serve as
a resource for researchers in the field, who may use it to simulate and analyze different scenarios.
Thirdly, the Python code developed in this project for automating new scenario creation from the
base scenario can be effectively utilized for further studies to investigate the optimal placement of
digitized secondary substations in different distribution grid types.
8.2
Limitations and Future directions
Although the study contributes towards optimizing the planning and rollout of digitized secondary
substations, however the thesis presents only a case study, further investigation and improvement
are necessary. Firstly, the key observations from this study have been limited to a few important
influence drivers, and it is essential to consider other factors that can affect the optimal placement
and prioritization of grid types for a digitized secondary substation. For instance, the sensitivity
analysis of grid towards cable types revealed that feeder characteristics such as location of one
tie points, cable length, number of substation etc. can impact the optimal placement of digitized
secondary substations and the benefits achieved in terms of minimizing disruptions in energy sup-
ply. This indicates that future studies should show the correlation of the input drivers based on
statistical analysis which incorporates correlation between ENS observed and increase in cable
length, number of substations, other key influence drivers and their layouts which constitute the
grid topology. Therefore, a more comprehensive assessment of these factors is required to improve
the accuracy and robustness of the proposed framework. Secondly, the study’s reliability assess-
ment was limited to one year, and did not account for the impact of cable failure probabilities. As
the cable failure probabilities increase over time, using an average failure frequency for the cables
may not provide a clear picture of line failures in the MV network. To improve the current model, a
possible approach would be to introduce age distribution for the cable types and perform reliability
simulations for their lifetimes. Further the other factors contributing to failure of cables such as
overloading, environmental factors such as temperature, moisture, humidity, mechanical damages,
manufacturing defects etc. need to be also taken into consideration. Therefore, future research
can consider incorporating all these factors in the reliability assessment to enhance the accuracy
and applicability of the proposed framework. Thirdly, the study assumes a fixed capacity for the
loads and the renewable resources such as PV, EVs and WTs, whereas their integration is typically
a gradual process over time. Therefore, to accurately reflect the impact of increasing load and
generation units on the distribution grid, future research should consider incorporating dynamic
capacities into the proposed framework. A possible suggestion for future researchers using this
workflow would be to investigate the load and generation scaling options provided by PowerFac-
tory to model the gradual increase of load and renewable energy capacity over time. Fourthly,
the benefits of optimally placing multiple digitized secondary substation into a feeder simultane-
ously can also be investigated. The optimization method developed in this thesis is incapable of
optimizing the placement of multiple digitized secondary substation. However, placing multiple
digitized secondary substations can help to evenly split the network and optimize the placement
of the substations from a reliability perspective [13]. Furthermore, other optimization techniques
that might be more efficient and better suited for the specific problem requirements should also
be considered. Finally, optimal placement of digitized secondary substation based on ENS is only
one part of the whole optimization. The combination of multiple criteria such as state estimation
estimation, data collection need to be also taken into consideration for more accurate and realistic
insight into optimal placement of digitized secondary substations and prioritization of grids.
